# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Configuration Hot-Reload Patterns Across K8s and Prometheus

## Your Task

Find Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes and prometheus/prometheus that implement configuration hot-reload (no process restart): the file watcher setup, the config diff detection, and the atomic config swap that applies new config without dropping connections.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

59-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of configuration hot-reload implementations in Kubernetes and Prometheus. Here's a summary of the findings:

## Key Implementation Files Found:

**Kubernetes (5 core files):**
- Dynamic certificate/CA content watchers using fsnotify
- Hash-based encryption config diff detection  
- Atomic config swap via `sync/atomic.Value`
- Work queue-based reload orchestration

**Prometheus (10 core files):**
- File discovery with fsnotify watching
- SHA256 checksum-based config diff detection
- Distributed `ApplyConfig()` methods for atomic subsystem updates
- No process restart - connections preserve their config state

## Implementation Patterns:

1. **File Watcher Setup**: Both use `github.com/fsnotify/fsnotify` with select loops handling Create/Write/Remove/Rename events

2. **Config Diff Detection**: 
   - Kubernetes: `bytes.Equal()` and SHA256 hash comparison
   - Prometheus: SHA256 of main + referenced files (handles atomic writes via glob)

3. **Atomic Config Swap**:
   - Kubernetes: `atomic.Value` for TLS config, served via `GetConfigForClient()` callback
   - Prometheus: Work queue guarantees + `ApplyConfig()` methods per subsystem

4. **No Restart Pattern**: New requests get new config immediately, existing connections continue with old config until completion

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed file paths, symbol names, call chains, and narrative explanations.

Kubernetes Implementation\\n\\n**File Watcher Setup:**\\nKubernetes uses `github.com/fsnotify/fsnotify` for watching file changes. The pattern is demonstrated in three key files:\\n\\n1. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/dynamiccertificates/dynamic_cafile_content.go` - Implements `watchCAFile()` method that creates an fsnotify.Watcher, adds the CA file to watch, and handles fsnotify.Events in a select loop. Clients read via `CurrentCABundleContent()` which calls `caBundle.Load()`.\\n\\n2. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/dynamiccertificates/tlsconfig.go` - The `syncCerts()` method:\\n   - Calls `newTLSContent()` to build new TLS config\\n   - Uses `newContent.Equal(c.currentlyServedContent)` to detect changes\\n   - Parses new certs into a cloned base TLS config\\n   - Atomically swaps config via `c.currentServingTLSConfig.Store(newTLSConfigCopy)` (line 227)\\n   - Uses `GetConfigForClient()` callback to serve latest config without restarting TLS listeners\\n\\nThe key pattern: no process restart, existing connections continue using the old config, new connections immediately get the updated config.\\n\\n### Prometheus Implementation\\n\\n**File Watcher Setup:**\\nPrometheus also uses fsnotify for file discovery:\\n\\n1. `discovery/file/file.go` - The `watchFiles()` method sets watches on configured file paths and directories. The `Run()` method creates `fsnotify.NewWatcher()`, calls `watchFiles()`, then enters select loop handling watcher.Events, ticker.C (periodic refresh), and watcher.Errors. Non-chmod events trigger `refresh()` to re-read target files.\\n\\n**Config Diff Detection:**\\nPrometheus uses SHA256-based checksum for detecting configuration changes:\\n\\n1. `config/reload.go` - The `GenerateChecksum()` function:\\n   - Reads main YAML configuration file\\n   - Parses for external file references (rule_files, scrape_config_files)\\n   - Generates SHA256 hash of main config content\\n   - For each referenced file matching glob patterns, appends to hash: file prefix, file path, and file content\\n   - Returns hex-encoded checksum\\n   - Handles atomic file writes correctly via glob matching\\n\\n2. `cmd/prometheus/main.go` - The reload loop:\\n   - After successful reload, calls `config.GenerateChecksum()` to get new checksum\\n   - On auto-reload polling interval, compares current checksum with stored checksum\\n   - Only triggers `reloadConfig()` if checksum differs\\n   - This avoids redundant parsing/validation when config unchanged\\n\\n**Atomic Config Swap:**\\nPrometheus distributes config changes to multiple subsystems via `ApplyConfig()` methods:\\n\\n1. `cmd/prometheus/main.go` - The `reloadConfig()` function:\\n   - Loads config via `config.LoadFile()`\\n   - Iterates through reloader functions (scrape manager, remote storage, alerting, rules, etc.)\\n   - Each reloader's `ApplyConfig(conf)` method handles its portion of configuration\\n   - If any reloader fails, entire reload fails and old config remains active\\n   - Sets success metrics regardless, allowing monitoring of reload status\\n\\n2. `scrape/manager.go` - ApplyConfig pattern:\\n   - Uses `reflect.DeepEqual(sp.config, cfg)` to detect scrape config changes per job\\n   - Uses buffered channel `canReload` to limit concurrent pool reloads\\n   - Spawns goroutine per pool to call `sp.reload(cfg)`\\n   - Deletes removed pools, updates changed pools in parallel\\n   - Returns error if any pool reload fails\\n\\n3. `scrape/scrape.go` - The `reload()` method:\\n   - Updates pool's config reference\\n   - Creates new HTTP client from updated config\\n   - Calls `restartLoops()` with reuse flag\\n   - In `restartLoops()`: for each existing scrape loop, either reuses scrape cache or creates new one\\n   - Spawns new scrape loop with updated config but preserves target state and active connections\\n   - Closes old HTTP client after new loops started\\n   - This ensures no dropped metrics during scrape config changes\\n\\n4. `tsdb/db.go` - ApplyConfig applies storage config changes:\\n   - Updates retention duration atomically via `atomic.Store()`\\n   - Updates exemplar and out-of-order time window settings\\n   - Calls `head.ApplyConfig()` for in-memory metrics changes\\n\\n5. `notifier/manager.go` - ApplyConfig for alertmanager discovery:\\n   - Applies new alerting configuration\\n   - Uses hash matching to preserve existing send loops when possible\\n   - Only stops/creates alertmanager connections for changed configs\\n\\nKey Prometheus pattern: Config hash drives reload decisions \u2192 Single `reloadConfig()` function parses once \u2192 Multiple `ApplyConfig()` methods atomically update each subsystem \u2192 No process restart, existing scrape loops and queries continue uninterrupted.\\n\\n### Common Patterns\\n\\nBoth Kubernetes and Prometheus implement:\\n1. **File Watchers**: fsnotify for event-driven reloads\\n2. **Diff Detection**: Content hashing (SHA256/bytes.Equal) for fast change detection  \\n3. **Two-Stage Validation**: Quick hash check, then detailed validation to prevent TOCTOU race conditions\\n4. **Work Queues**: Backoff/retry semantics for failed reloads\\n5. **Atomic Swaps**: Go's atomic.Value or single-threaded guarantees to swap config without locks\\n6. **No Process Restart**: New connections/requests get new config, existing ones continue with old config until completion\\n7. **Error Handling**: Failed reloads keep old config active, record metrics, and retry asynchronously\"\n}\n",

The pattern is demonstrated in three key files:\\n\\n1. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/dynamiccertificates/dynamic_cafile_content.go` - Implements `watchCAFile()` method that creates an fsnotify.Watcher, adds the CA file to watch, and handles fsnotify.Events in a select loop. The hash serves as a cheap check to determine if the file has changed.\\n\\n3. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/encryptionconfig/controller/controller.go` - The `processEncryptionConfig()` method performs a two-stage diff check: first comparing content hash before loading (fast), then comparing the loaded configuration's hash after loading to avoid TOCTOU issues.\\n\\n**Atomic Config Swap:**\\nKubernetes uses Go's `sync/atomic.Value` for atomic config updates:\\n\\n1. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/dynamiccertificates/dynamic_cafile_content.go` - Stores parsed CA bundle in `atomic.Value` with `caBundle.Store(caBundleAndVerifier)`. Clients read via `CurrentCABundleContent()` which calls `caBundle.Load()`.\\n\\n2. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/dynamiccertificates/tlsconfig.go` - The `syncCerts()` method:\\n   - Calls `newTLSContent()` to build new TLS config\\n   - Uses `newContent.Equal(c.currentlyServedContent)` to detect changes\\n   - Parses new certs into a cloned base TLS config\\n   - Atomically swaps config via `c.currentServingTLSConfig.Store(newTLSConfigCopy)` (line 227)\\n   - Uses `GetConfigForClient()` callback to serve latest config without restarting TLS listeners\\n\\nThe key pattern: no process restart, existing connections continue using the old config, new connections immediately get the updated config.\\n\\n### Prometheus Implementation\\n\\n**File Watcher Setup:**\\nPrometheus also uses fsnotify for file discovery:\\n\\n1. `discovery/file/file.go` - The `watchFiles()` method sets watches on configured file paths and directories. The `Run()` method creates `fsnotify.NewWatcher()`, calls `watchFiles()`, then enters select loop handling watcher.Events, ticker.C (periodic refresh), and watcher.Errors. Non-chmod events trigger `refresh()` to re-read target files.\\n\\n**Config Diff Detection:**\\nPrometheus uses SHA256-based checksum for detecting configuration changes:\\n\\n1. `config/reload.go` - The `GenerateChecksum()` function:\\n   - Reads main YAML configuration file\\n   - Parses for external file references (rule_files, scrape_config_files)\\n   - Generates SHA256 hash of main config content\\n   - For each referenced file matching glob patterns, appends to hash: file prefix, file path, and file content\\n   - Returns hex-encoded checksum\\n   - Handles atomic file writes correctly via glob matching\\n\\n2. `cmd/prometheus/main.go` - The reload loop:\\n   - After successful reload, calls `config.GenerateChecksum()` to get new checksum\\n   - On auto-reload polling interval, compares current checksum with stored checksum\\n   - Only triggers `reloadConfig()` if checksum differs\\n   - This avoids redundant parsing/validation when config unchanged\\n\\n**Atomic Config Swap:**\\nPrometheus distributes config changes to multiple subsystems via `ApplyConfig()` methods:\\n\\n1. `cmd/prometheus/main.go` - The `reloadConfig()` function:\\n   - Loads config via `config.LoadFile()`\\n   - Iterates through reloader functions (scrape manager, remote storage, alerting, rules, etc.)\\n   - Each reloader's `ApplyConfig(conf)` method handles its portion of configuration\\n   - If any reloader fails, entire reload fails and old config remains active\\n   - Sets success metrics regardless, allowing monitoring of reload status\\n\\n2. `scrape/manager.go` - ApplyConfig pattern:\\n   - Uses `reflect.DeepEqual(sp.config, cfg)` to detect scrape config changes per job\\n   - Uses buffered channel `canReload` to limit concurrent pool reloads\\n   - Spawns goroutine per pool to call `sp.reload(cfg)`\\n   - Deletes removed pools, updates changed pools in parallel\\n   - Returns error if any pool reload fails\\n\\n3. `scrape/scrape.go` - The `reload()` method:\\n   - Updates pool's config reference\\n   - Creates new HTTP client from updated config\\n   - Calls `restartLoops()` with reuse flag\\n   - In `restartLoops()`: for each existing scrape loop, either reuses scrape cache or creates new one\\n   - Spawns new scrape loop with updated config but preserves target state and active connections\\n   - Closes old HTTP client after new loops started\\n   - This ensures no dropped metrics during scrape config changes\\n\\n4. `tsdb/db.go` - ApplyConfig applies storage config changes:\\n   - Updates retention duration atomically via `atomic.Store()`\\n   - Updates exemplar and out-of-order time window settings\\n   - Calls `head.ApplyConfig()` for in-memory metrics changes\\n\\n5. `notifier/manager.go` - ApplyConfig for alertmanager discovery:\\n   - Applies new alerting configuration\\n   - Uses hash matching to preserve existing send loops when possible\\n   - Only stops/creates alertmanager connections for changed configs\\n\\nKey Prometheus pattern: Config hash drives reload decisions \u2192 Single `reloadConfig()` function parses once \u2192 Multiple `ApplyConfig()` methods atomically update each subsystem \u2192 No process restart, existing scrape loops and queries continue uninterrupted.\\n\\n### Common Patterns\\n\\nBoth Kubernetes and Prometheus implement:\\n1. **File Watchers**: fsnotify for event-driven reloads\\n2. **Diff Detection**: Content hashing (SHA256/bytes.Equal) for fast change detection  \\n3. **Two-Stage Validation**: Quick hash check, then detailed validation to prevent TOCTOU race conditions\\n4. **Work Queues**: Backoff/retry semantics for failed reloads\\n5. **Atomic Swaps**: Go's atomic.Value or single-threaded guarantees to swap config without locks\\n6. **No Process Restart**: New connections/requests get new config, existing ones continue with old config until completion\\n7. **Error Handling**: Failed reloads keep old config active, record metrics, and retry asynchronously\"\n}\n",
